beginner
4 min
The Fourth Argument on Existence and Its Answer
Sanusi presents the fourth argument and its answer on existence being additional to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument that questions whether existence is identical to the essence of the Necessary Being or an additional attribute, and how Sanusi answers by distinguishing between absolute and specific being.

Core Idea
The Necessary Being is specific abstract being, not absolute existence.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a refined objection from those who argue about the relationship between existence and the essence of the Necessary Being. He systematically considers what 'being' could mean, showing that each alternative leads to an absurdity except one: that existence is additional to the essence. The answer clarifies that this addition is accepted only for absolute existence, not for the specific existence of the Necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice how Sanusi lists multiple conditional statements about the meaning of 'being' (al-kawn).
The passage is dense with logical possibilities; take your time.
2
Identify the four possibilities
The argument considers four scenarios: (1) the Necessary is identical to absolute existence, (2) it is being with the condition of abstraction, (3) it is being conditioned by abstraction, (4) it is other than being-in-entities. For each, note the consequence.
The fourth scenario branches into sub-possibilities.
3
Understand the answer
After the argument, Sanusi gives the answer: the Necessary is the specific abstract being that differs from other beings. The dispute about addition exists only for absolute being, not for this specific being.
4
Test your understanding with the quiz
Answer the multiple-choice question to check if you grasped the key consequence of the first possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : الواجب إن كان نفس الكون في الأعيان - أعني الوجود المطلق لزم تعدد الواجب ضرورة أن وجود زيد غير وجود عمرو، وإن كان هو الكون مع القيد التجرد لزم تركب الواجب من الوجود والتجرد مع أنه عدمي لا يصلح جزءاً للواجب، أو بشرط التجرد لزم أن يكون الواجب واجباً لذاته، بل بشرطه الذي هو التجرد، وإن كان غير الكون في الأعيان فإن كان بدون الكون في الأعيان فمحال ضرورة أنه لا يعقل الوجود بدون الكون، وإن كان مع الكون فإما أن يكون الكون داخلا فيه وهو محال ضرورة امتناع تركب الواجب، أو خارجاً عنه وهو المطلوب، لأن معناه زيادة الوجود على ما هو حقيقة الواجب . والجواب : أنه نفس الكون الخاص المجرد المخالف الأكوان، ولا نزاع في زيادة الكون المطلق عليه .
The fourth: If the necessary being is identical to being-in-entities (al-kawn fi al-a'yan) - I mean absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), then multiplicity of the necessary would necessarily follow because the existence of Zayd is not the existence of 'Amr. And if it is being (al-kawn) with the condition of abstraction (al-tajarrud), then composition of the necessary would necessarily follow from existence and abstraction, while abstraction is non-existent and not fit to be a part of the necessary. Or if it is conditioned by abstraction, then the necessary would be necessary by itself, but by its condition which is abstraction. And if it is other than being-in-entities, then if it is without being-in-entities, it is impossible necessarily because existence cannot be conceived without being. And if it is with being, then either being is included in it, which is impossible due to the impossibility of composition of the necessary, or it is external to it, which is what is sought, because its meaning is the addition of existence to what is the reality of the necessary. The answer: It is the specific abstract being (al-kawn al-khas al-mujarrad) that differs from other beings, and there is no dispute about the addition of absolute being (al-kawn al-mutlaq) to it.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument regarding whether existence (wujud) is identical to the essence of the Necessary Being (al-wajib) or additional to it. The argument proceeds by considering various possibilities for what 'being' (al-kawn) might mean. First, if the Necessary is identical to absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq) as found in entities, then there would be multiple necessary beings because the existence of Zayd is different from that of 'Amr. Second, if it is being with the condition of abstraction, then the Necessary would be composed of existence and abstraction, but abstraction is a privation (amr 'adami) and cannot be a part of the Necessary. Third, if it is conditioned by abstraction, then the Necessary would be necessary by itself, but only by virtue of the condition of abstraction, not by its essence. Fourth, if it is other than being-in-entities, then either it is entirely without being-in-entities (impossible) or it encompasses being-in-entities either as included (leading to composition) or as external (the desired outcome, meaning existence is additional to the essence). The answer states that the Necessary is the specific abstract being that differs from other beings, and there is no dispute about the addition of absolute being (al-kawn al-mutlaq) to it.

Key Terms
الواجب
الكون في الأعيان
الوجود المطلق
التجرد
الكون الخاص المجرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fourth argument proves that existence is additional to the essence of the Necessary Being in an absolute sense.
Correction: The argument's conclusion that existence is additional only applies to absolute being (al-kawn al-mutlaq); the Necessary Being itself is a specific abstract being (al-kawn al-khas al-mujarrad), about which there is no dispute of addition.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth argument, what would happen if the Necessary Being were identical to absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq) as found in entities?
A) It would be composed of parts.
B) It would be impossible.
C) There would be multiple necessary beings.
D) It would be conditioned by abstraction.

Key Takeaway
The Necessary Being is specific abstract existence, not the general absolute existence, and the debate about existence as an addition applies only to the general concept.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you unconsciously treat God’s existence as just one more being among many—comparable to the things you see and touch? If you truly internalized that His existence is absolutely unique and incomparable, what would you need to change in your priorities or worship right now?
?
The argument shows that thinking of God’s existence as a universal category leads to absurdity. Have you ever assumed that God ‘exists’ in the same way you do, only more powerful? What specific thought pattern would you need to uproot to begin thinking of His existence as utterly unlike anything else?

The Fifth Argument: Existence Known, Essence Unknown
Sanusi presents and refutes the fifth argument about existence being known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the argument that existence must be additional to the essence because existence is known necessarily while the essence is unknown.

Core Idea
Absolute existence is known; specific existence is the unknown essence.

Sanusi now presents a fifth argument against those who claim existence is additional to the essence. The argument relies on the fact that existence is known by necessity while the essence of God is unknown. But Sanusi shows that this only proves the addition of absolute existence, which is not in dispute. This lesson walks through the argument and its precise answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the flow of argument and response.
Notice that the answer distinguishes absolute existence from specific existence.
2
Identify the distinction
Identify the key distinction between absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq) and specific existence (al-wujud al-khas). Understand how this distinction dissolves the argument.
The argument only works if it conflates these two.
3
Reflect on the point
Ask yourself: What is the real dispute? The answer clarifies that the dispute is only about the addition of specific existence, not absolute existence.
This shows the argument is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : الوجود معلوم بالضرورة، وحقيقة الواجب غير معلومة اتفاقاً وغير المعلوم (هو) غير المعلوم ضرورة والجواب : أن المعلوم هو الوجود المطلق للمغاير للخاص الذي هو نفس الحقيقة، وإلى هذه الأجوبة أشار بقوله : لا نزاع في زيادة الوجود المطلق أي على ماهية الواجب وإنما النزاع في زيادة وجوده الخاص، وما ذكر من الوجوه لا يدل عليها .
The fifth: Existence (al-wujud) is known by necessity, and the reality of the necessary (haqiqat al-wajib) is unknown by agreement, and what is unknown is other than what is known by necessity. The answer: That which is known is the absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq) which is other than the specific existence that is the very reality. And to these answers he pointed by his saying: There is no dispute about the addition of absolute existence, i.e., over the quiddity (mahiyya) of the necessary; rather the dispute is about the addition of His specific existence, and what has been mentioned of the proofs does not indicate it.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument: Existence (al-wujud) is known necessarily, but the reality (haqiqa) of the Necessary Being is unknown by agreement (among theologians). Since the unknown cannot be the same as the known, existence must be additional to the essence. The answer refutes this: what is known necessarily is absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq), which is distinct from the specific existence that is identical to the essence of the Necessary. Therefore, the unknown essence is the specific existence, not the absolute existence. The author then cites his own statement that there is no dispute about the addition of absolute existence to the quiddity; the real dispute is about the addition of specific existence. The arguments presented (like this fifth one) do not prove the addition of specific existence.

Key Terms
الوجود (al-wujud)
المعلوم بالضرورة (al-ma'lum bil-darura)
حقيقة الواجب (haqiqat al-wajib)
الوجود المطلق (al-wujud al-mutlaq)
الوجود الخاص (al-wujud al-khas)
الماهية (al-mahiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fifth argument proves that existence is additional to the essence of God because existence is known and essence is unknown.
Correction: The argument only shows that absolute existence is additional to quiddity, which is not disputed. The specific existence, identical to the essence, remains unknown.

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the fifth argument, what is known by necessity?
A) The specific existence of the Necessary
B) Absolute existence (al-wujud al-mutlaq)
C) The reality of the Necessary
D) The quiddity of the Necessary

Key Takeaway
The fifth argument fails because it conflates absolute existence (known) with specific existence (unknown), and the addition of absolute existence is not in dispute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know with certainty that God exists, yet His true essence remains hidden from you. How does this awareness change the way you approach your worship and your quest to know Him?
?
This lesson warns against confusing a general concept (absolute existence) with the specific reality of God. In your own life, where might you be settling for a vague intellectual knowledge of God rather than pursuing the specific, personal relationship He deserves?
?
The arguer's mistake was conflating what is universally known with what is uniquely true of God. Have you ever reduced God to a category or concept, treating Him as just another 'existent' rather than the utterly unique Being He is? What does this tell you about the need for humility in theology?
